```spl
-- Recipe 02: Ollama Proxy
-- General-purpose LLM query — proxy any prompt to any adapter/model.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/02_ollama_proxy/proxy.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 prompt="Explain quantum computing in one sentence"
--   spl run cookbook/02_ollama_proxy/proxy.spl --adapter ollama -m llama3.2 prompt="Write a haiku about coding"
--   spl run cookbook/02_ollama_proxy/proxy.spl --adapter ollama -m mistral prompt="What is 2+2?"
--   spl run cookbook/02_ollama_proxy/proxy.spl --adapter anthropic prompt="Summarise the history of AI"
--
-- Parameters:
--   prompt  (required)  The user prompt / question

PROMPT ollama_proxy
SELECT
    system_role('You are a helpful, knowledgeable assistant.'),
    context.prompt AS prompt
GENERATE answer(prompt)
```

     | Model: gemma3

-- Recipe 03: Multilingual Greeting
-- Greet in any language — demonstrates parametric context with lang.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/03_multilingual/multilingual.spl --adapter ollama user_input="hello wen" lang="Chinese"
--   spl run cookbook/03_multilingual/multilingual.spl --adapter ollama user_input="hello wen" lang="French"
--   spl run cookbook/03_multilingual/multilingual.spl --adapter ollama user_input="hello wen" lang="Japanese"
--   spl run cookbook/03_multilingual/multilingual.spl --adapter ollama user_input="hello wen" lang="Spanish"

PROMPT multilingual_greeting
SELECT
    system_role('You are a friendly assistant. Respond in the language specified.'),
    context.user_input AS input,
    context.lang AS lang
GENERATE greeting(input, lang)
```

     | 
```spl
-- Recipe 04: Model Showdown
-- Same prompt to multiple Ollama models — compare responses side-by-side.
-- Uses parallel CTEs instead of a bash loop for a pure-SPL implementation.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/04_model_showdown/showdown.spl --adapter ollama \
--       prompt="What is the meaning of life?"
--   spl run cookbook/04_model_showdown/showdown.spl --adapter ollama \
--       prompt="Explain recursion in 3 sentences" \
--       model_1=gemma3 model_2=llama3.2 model_3=mistral

CREATE FUNCTION compare_responses(
    prompt TEXT,
    model_1 TEXT, answer_1 TEXT,
    model_2 TEXT, answer_2 TEXT,
    model_3 TEXT, answer_3 TEXT
) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a neutral evaluator comparing responses from three AI models.

Prompt given to all models: "{prompt}"

First, reproduce each model's raw response exactly as given, formatted like this:

=== {model_1} ===
{answer_1}

=== {model_2} ===
{answer_2}

=== {model_3} ===
{answer_3}

Then provide your evaluation. For each model briefly assess:
- Response quality
- Key strengths or weaknesses

Conclude with which model gave the most helpful answer and why.
$$;

WORKFLOW model_showdown
    INPUT:
        @prompt  TEXT DEFAULT 'What is the meaning of life?',
        @model_1 TEXT DEFAULT 'gemma3',
        @model_2 TEXT DEFAULT 'phi3',
        @model_3 TEXT DEFAULT 'qwen2.5'
    OUTPUT: @comparison TEXT
DO
    -- Run the same prompt against all three models in parallel CTEs
    WITH
        response_1 AS (
            PROMPT ask_model_1
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a helpful, knowledgeable assistant.'),
                @prompt AS prompt
            GENERATE answer(prompt)
            USING MODEL @model_1
        ),
        response_2 AS (
            PROMPT ask_model_2
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a helpful, knowledgeable assistant.'),
                @prompt AS prompt
            GENERATE answer(prompt)
            USING MODEL @model_2
        ),
        response_3 AS (
            PROMPT ask_model_3
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a helpful, knowledgeable assistant.'),
                @prompt AS prompt
            GENERATE answer(prompt)
            USING MODEL @model_3
        )
    SELECT
        response_1.answer AS answer_1,
        response_2.answer AS answer_2,
        response_3.answer AS answer_3
    INTO @answer_1, @answer_2, @answer_3

    -- Judge all three responses together
    GENERATE compare_responses(
        @prompt,
        @model_1, @answer_1,
        @model_2, @answer_2,
        @model_3, @answer_3
    ) INTO @comparison

    COMMIT @comparison WITH
        status   = 'complete',
        model_1  = @model_1,
        model_2  = @model_2,
        model_3  = @model_3

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        COMMIT 'One or more models failed to respond.' WITH status = 'error'
END
```

While phi3's response is structured and well-organized, it feels a bit generic or cliche at times. qwen2.5's response has some strengths, but its awkward translation and inconsistent English-Chinese mix hold it back.

```spl
-- SPL 2.0: Self-Refine Pattern
-- Iteratively improves output through critique and refinement

WORKFLOW self_refine
  INPUT: 
    @task text,
    @max_iterations integer default 5
  OUTPUT: @result text
DO
  @iteration := 0
  --  @max_iterations := 5

  -- Initial draft
  GENERATE draft(@task) INTO @current

  -- Iterative refinement loop
  WHILE @iteration < @max_iterations DO
    GENERATE critique(@current) INTO @feedback

    EVALUATE @feedback
      WHEN 'satisfactory' THEN
        COMMIT @current WITH status = 'complete', iterations = @iteration
      OTHERWISE
        GENERATE refined(@current, @feedback) INTO @current
        @iteration := @iteration + 1
    END
  END

  -- If loop exhausted, commit best effort
  COMMIT @current WITH status = 'max_iterations', iterations = @iteration

EXCEPTION
  WHEN MaxIterationsReached THEN
    COMMIT @current WITH status = 'partial'
  WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
    COMMIT @current WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```

     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 3

```spl
-- SPL 2.0: ReAct Agent — Population Growth
-- Fetch a country's population for the past two years via WebSearch,
-- then compute year-over-year growth rate using a Python tool (no LLM math).
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/06_react_agent/react_agent.spl \
--       --adapter claude_cli -m claude-sonnet-4-6 \
--       --allowed-tools WebSearch \
--       --tools cookbook/06_react_agent/tools.py \
--       country="France"

-- Tight prompt for search_population: return only the number, no narration.
CREATE FUNCTION search_population(country TEXT, year INT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Use WebSearch to find the total population of {country} for the year {year}.

Return ONLY the population as a plain integer with no commas, spaces, or text.
Example of valid output: 1409670000
No explanation. No units. No markdown. Just the number.
$$;

-- SPL PROCEDURE: search the web for a country's population in a specific year.
PROCEDURE search_population(country TEXT, year INT)
RETURNS TEXT
DO
  GENERATE search_population(country, year) INTO @result
  COMMIT @result
END

-- calc_growth_rate is a Python tool registered from tools.py via --tools.
-- CALL routes to Python directly — deterministic, zero LLM cost.

-- Tight prompt for growth_report: plain narrative, no tool use, no file writes.
CREATE FUNCTION growth_report(country TEXT, year_prev TEXT, pop_prev TEXT, year_curr TEXT, pop_curr TEXT, growth_rate TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Write a concise 2-3 sentence population growth report for {country}.

Data:
- {year_prev} population: {pop_prev}
- {year_curr} population: {pop_curr}
- Year-over-year growth rate: {growth_rate}%

Plain prose only. No markdown headers. No file creation. No tool use. Just the narrative.
$$;

WORKFLOW population_growth
  INPUT: 
    @country TEXT DEFAULT 'China',
    @year_curr integer default 2023
  OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
  @year_prev := @year_curr - 1
  -- @year_curr := 2024

  -- Step 1: Fetch population for each year via WebSearch
  CALL search_population(@country, @year_prev) INTO @pop_prev
  CALL search_population(@country, @year_curr) INTO @pop_curr

  -- Step 2: Compute growth rate — routed to Python tool, not LLM
  CALL calc_growth_rate(@pop_prev, @pop_curr) INTO @growth_rate

  -- Step 3: Compose the final human-readable report
  GENERATE growth_report(@country, @year_prev, @pop_prev, @year_curr, @pop_curr, @growth_rate) INTO @report

  COMMIT @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
  WHEN SearchFailed THEN
    GENERATE search_error_report(@country) INTO @report
    COMMIT @report WITH status = 'error'
END
```
     | 
     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 3
     | Tokens: 186 in / 97 out
     | Latency: 27112ms
     | ------------------------------------------------------------
```output
France's population grew from approximately 68.1 million in 2022 to 68.3 million in 2023, an increase of roughly 222,000 people. This modest year-over-year growth rate of 0.33% reflects a pattern of slow but steady demographic expansion. At this pace, France remains one of Europe's more demographically stable nations, though the rate falls well below the global average.
```

     |   @growth_rate = 0.3269

Explain how encryption works
```
     | 
```spl
-- SPL 2.0: Safe Generation with Exception Handling
-- Demonstrates LLM-specific error handling patterns

WORKFLOW safe_generation
  INPUT: @prompt text
  OUTPUT: @result text
  SECURITY: CLASSIFICATION: internal
DO
  GENERATE response(@prompt) INTO @result

  -- Quality check via semantic evaluation (LLM-as-judge)
  GENERATE quality_assess(@result) INTO @quality

  EVALUATE @quality
    WHEN 'high_quality' THEN
      COMMIT @result WITH status = 'high_quality'
    WHEN 'acceptable' THEN
      GENERATE improved(@result, @prompt) INTO @result
      COMMIT @result WITH status = 'refined'
    OTHERWISE
      COMMIT @result WITH status = 'best_effort'
  END

EXCEPTION
  WHEN HallucinationDetected THEN
    GENERATE response(@prompt) INTO @result
    COMMIT @result WITH status = 'conservative'

  WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
    RETRY WITH temperature = 0.1

  WHEN RefusalToAnswer THEN
    COMMIT @prompt WITH status = 'refused'

  WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
    COMMIT @result WITH status = 'truncated'
END
```
     | 
     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 3
     | Tokens: 937 in / 816 out
     | Latency: 10169ms
     | ------------------------------------------------------------
```output
Encryption is the process of converting plaintext (readable data) into ciphertext (unreadable data) to ensure secure communication over an insecure channel. Here's a simplified explanation of how encryption works:

**The Encryption Process**

1. **Key Generation**: An encryption algorithm uses a secret key to encrypt and decrypt the data.
2. **Data Encapsulation**: The plaintext data is encapsulated within a block, which may include additional information such as headers or padding.
3. **Encryption**: The encryption algorithm applies a series of mathematical operations to the encapsulated data using the secret key. These operations can include substitutions, rearrangements, and other transformations.
4. **Ciphertext Generation**: The resulting encrypted data is called ciphertext.

**Types of Encryption Algorithms**

1. **Symmetric Key Encryption**: Uses the same key for both encryption and decryption (e.g., AES).
2. **Asymmetric Key Encryption**: Uses a pair of keys: one for encryption (public) and another for decryption (private).

**How Encryption Ensures Security**

Encryption provides several benefits:

1. **Confidentiality**: Only authorized parties with the correct decryption key can access the ciphertext.
2. **Integrity**: Changes to the plaintext data are detectable, ensuring that the data has not been tampered with.
3. **Authenticity**: The encryption process ensures that the data comes from a trusted source.

**Common Encryption Techniques**

1. **Block Ciphers**: Divide data into fixed-size blocks and apply encryption operations to each block (e.g., AES).
2. **Stream Ciphers**: Process data in a continuous stream, applying encryption operations to individual bytes or bits.
3. **Hash Functions**: Generate a fixed-length hash value from variable-sized input data.

**Best Practices for Encryption**

1. **Use Strong Keys**: Choose keys with sufficient entropy ( randomness) and length.
2. **Use Secure Algorithms**: Select algorithms that are widely accepted and regularly updated for security patches.
3. **Store Keys Securely**: Protect encryption keys from unauthorized access using secure storage mechanisms.

By understanding how encryption works, you can effectively protect sensitive data and ensure the confidentiality, integrity, and authenticity of your communications.

```spl
-- Recipe 09: Chain of Thought
-- Multi-step reasoning: Research → Analyze → Summarize
-- Each GENERATE feeds into the next via workflow variables.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/09_chain_of_thought/chain.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 topic="distributed AI inference"
--   spl run cookbook/09_chain_of_thought/chain.spl --adapter ollama -m llama3.2 topic="quantum computing"

WORKFLOW chain_of_thought
    INPUT: @topic TEXT
    OUTPUT: @summary TEXT
DO
    -- Step 1: Research
    GENERATE research(@topic) INTO @research

    -- Step 2: Analyze
    GENERATE analyze(@research) INTO @analysis

    -- Step 3: Summarize
    GENERATE summarize(@analysis) INTO @summary

    COMMIT @summary WITH status = 'complete'
END
```

**Key Points:**

```
     | ------------------------------------------------------------
     | Variables:
     |   @topic = distributed AI inference
     |   @research = **Distributed AI Inference Research**
     | 
     | Distributed AI inference refers to the process of running machine learning models on multiple computing devices or nodes in a network, rather than relying on a single central processing unit (CPU). This approach can significantly speed up the training and inference processes for large datasets.
     | 
     | **Benefits:**
     | 
     | 1. **Scalability**: Distributed AI inference allows for scalability, enabling the model to be trained or run on many more data points.
     | 2. **Speedup**: By distributing the computational load across multiple nodes, each node can process a portion of the data individually, leading to faster processing times.
     | 3. **Fault tolerance**: If one node fails, others in the distributed system can continue running the computation without interruption.
     | 
     | **Key Challenges:**
     | 
     | 1. **Communication overhead**: Data must be transferred between nodes, which can lead to significant communication costs and slower overall performance.
     | 2. **Model synchronization**: Ensuring that all nodes have the same model parameters and are running the same version is crucial for consistency across the distributed system.
     | 3. **Resource allocation**: Efficiently distributing computational resources among nodes is essential to achieve optimal performance.
     | 
     | **Key Techniques:**
     | 
     | 1. **Parameter Server Architecture (PSA)**: A widely used approach where a central node, called the parameter server, stores model parameters and other data. All other nodes communicate with this parameter server.
     | 2. **Model Parallelism**: Dividing the model into separate components that can be processed by multiple nodes in parallel.
     | 3. **Data Parallelism**: Splitting the input data across multiple nodes to process it in parallel.
     | 
     | **Popular Distributed AI Inference Frameworks:**
     | 
     | 1. **Distributed TensorFlow**: An extension of TensorFlow, which provides a framework for building and training distributed machine learning models.
     | 2. **Hadoop MapReduce**: A widely used framework for processing large datasets by breaking them into smaller chunks and processing them in parallel across multiple nodes.
     | 3. **Apache Spark**: A unified analytics engine for large-scale data processing.
     | 
     | **Real-World Applications:**
     | 
     | 1. **Computer Vision**: Distributed AI inference can speed up object detection, image segmentation, and other computer vision tasks using models like YOLO and SegNet.
     | 2. **Natural Language Processing (NLP)**: Distributed AI inference can improve the performance of NLP models in applications such as text classification and language translation.
     | 
     | **Future Research Directions:**
     | 
     | 1. **Edge Computing**: Integrating distributed AI inference with edge computing, enabling real-time processing at the edge of the network.
     | 2. **Quantum-Inspired Optimization Algorithms**: Developing optimization algorithms inspired by quantum mechanics to improve performance and efficiency in distributed AI inference systems.
     | 3. **Explainability and Transparency**: Investigating methods to provide insights into how models are optimized and validated during distributed AI inference.
     | 
     | **Code Example:**
```python
import tensorflow as tf

# Define a simple neural network model
model = tf.keras.models.Sequential([
    tf.keras.layers.Dense(64, activation='relu', input_shape=(784,)),
    tf.keras.layers.Dense(10)
])

# Initialize the model in parameter server mode
ps = tf.keras.callbacks.ParameterServerModel(model)

# Define a worker node that runs inference on the model
def worker(node_id):
    # Get the model parameters from the parameter server
    params = ps.get_params()

    # Run inference using the model and input data
    output = model.predict(input_data, params=params)

    # Return the result to the parameter server
    return output

# Create a list of worker nodes
worker_nodes = [1, 2, 3]

# Run the distributed inference task
results = []
for node_id in worker_nodes:
    results.extend(worker(node_id))

print(results)
```

The `worker` function runs inference on the model using the input data provided by the model, while the `ps.get_params()` method retrieves the model parameters from the parameter server.

     cmd : spl run ./10_batch_test/batch_test.spl --adapter ollama

     | 
```spl
-- Recipe 10: Batch Test
-- Automated testing of key cookbook recipes across multiple models.
-- Uses parallel CTEs to fan out all recipe × model combinations at once,
-- then generates a structured PASS/FAIL report.
--
-- The bash script (batch_test.sh) is kept for CI/CD and shell-based pipelines.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/10_batch_test/batch_test.spl --adapter ollama
--   spl run cookbook/10_batch_test/batch_test.spl --adapter ollama \
--       model_1=gemma3 model_2=mistral

CREATE FUNCTION summarize_results(
    model_1 TEXT,
    model_2 TEXT,
    r1_name TEXT, r1_m1 TEXT, r1_m2 TEXT,
    r2_name TEXT, r2_m1 TEXT, r2_m2 TEXT,
    r3_name TEXT, r3_m1 TEXT, r3_m2 TEXT
) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a test reporter. Review the outputs below and produce a concise pass/fail report.

A result is PASS if the output is a non-empty, coherent response.
A result is FAIL if the output is empty, contains an error, or is clearly nonsensical.

Models under test: {model_1}, {model_2}

Recipe: {r1_name}
  {model_1}: {r1_m1}
  {model_2}: {r1_m2}

Recipe: {r2_name}
  {model_1}: {r2_m1}
  {model_2}: {r2_m2}

Recipe: {r3_name}
  {model_1}: {r3_m1}
  {model_2}: {r3_m2}

Format each line as:
  PASS  recipe_name  ({model})
  FAIL  recipe_name  ({model})

End with a summary line: "Results: X/Y passed, Z failed"
$$;

WORKFLOW batch_test
    INPUT:
        @model_1 TEXT DEFAULT 'gemma3',
        @model_2 TEXT DEFAULT 'llama3.2'
    OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
    -- Fan out all recipe × model combinations in parallel CTEs
    WITH
        -- Recipe 01: Hello World
        hello_m1 AS (
            PROMPT hello_world
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a helpful assistant. Say hello briefly.')
            GENERATE greeting()
            USING MODEL @model_1
        ),
        hello_m2 AS (
            PROMPT hello_world
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a helpful assistant. Say hello briefly.')
            GENERATE greeting()
            USING MODEL @model_2
        ),

        -- Recipe 02: Ollama Proxy
        proxy_m1 AS (
            PROMPT ollama_proxy
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a helpful, knowledgeable assistant.'),
                'hello' AS prompt
            GENERATE answer(prompt)
            USING MODEL @model_1
        ),
        proxy_m2 AS (
            PROMPT ollama_proxy
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a helpful, knowledgeable assistant.'),
                'hello' AS prompt
            GENERATE answer(prompt)
            USING MODEL @model_2
        ),

        -- Recipe 03: Multilingual
        multi_m1 AS (
            PROMPT multilingual
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a multilingual assistant.'),
                'hello' AS user_input,
                'English' AS lang
            GENERATE response(user_input, lang)
            USING MODEL @model_1
        ),
        multi_m2 AS (
            PROMPT multilingual
            SELECT
                system_role('You are a multilingual assistant.'),
                'hello' AS user_input,
                'English' AS lang
            GENERATE response(user_input, lang)
            USING MODEL @model_2
        )

    SELECT
        hello_m1.greeting  AS hello_m1,  hello_m2.greeting  AS hello_m2,
        proxy_m1.answer    AS proxy_m1,  proxy_m2.answer    AS proxy_m2,
        multi_m1.response  AS multi_m1,  multi_m2.response  AS multi_m2
    INTO @hello_m1, @hello_m2,
         @proxy_m1, @proxy_m2,
         @multi_m1, @multi_m2

    -- Generate the structured pass/fail report
    GENERATE summarize_results(
        @model_1, @model_2,
        '01_hello_world/hello.spl',        @hello_m1, @hello_m2,
        '02_ollama_proxy/proxy.spl',        @proxy_m1, @proxy_m2,
        '03_multilingual/multilingual.spl', @multi_m1, @multi_m2
    ) INTO @report

    COMMIT @report WITH
        status  = 'complete',
        model_1 = @model_1,
        model_2 = @model_2

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        COMMIT 'Batch test failed during generation.' WITH status = 'error'
END
```

```spl
-- Recipe 11: Debate Arena
-- Two LLM personas argue opposing sides of a topic, then a judge picks the winner.
-- Demonstrates multi-perspective reasoning, adversarial generation, and semantic evaluation.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/11_debate_arena/debate.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 topic="AI should be open-sourced"
--   spl run cookbook/11_debate_arena/debate.spl --adapter ollama -m llama3.2 topic="Remote work is better than office work"
--   spl run cookbook/11_debate_arena/debate.spl --adapter ollama topic="Tabs are better than spaces"

WORKFLOW debate_arena
    INPUT: 
        @topic TEXT,
        @max_rounds integer DEFAULT 3
    OUTPUT: @verdict TEXT
DO
    @round := 0
    -- @max_rounds := 3
    @pro_history := ''
    @con_history := ''

    -- Opening statements
    GENERATE pro_argument(@topic, 'opening statement') INTO @pro
    GENERATE con_argument(@topic, 'opening statement') INTO @con

    @pro_history := @pro
    @con_history := @con

    -- Rebuttal rounds
    WHILE @round < @max_rounds DO
        -- Pro rebuts Con's latest point
        GENERATE pro_argument(@topic, @con_history) INTO @pro_rebuttal
        @pro_history := @pro_history + '\n---\n' + @pro_rebuttal

        -- Con rebuts Pro's latest point
        GENERATE con_argument(@topic, @pro_history) INTO @con_rebuttal
        @con_history := @con_history + '\n---\n' + @con_rebuttal

        @round := @round + 1
    END

    -- Judge evaluates both sides
    GENERATE judge_debate(@topic, @pro_history, @con_history) INTO @verdict

    COMMIT @verdict WITH status = 'complete', rounds = @round

EXCEPTION
    WHEN MaxIterationsReached THEN
        GENERATE judge_debate(@topic, @pro_history, @con_history) INTO @verdict
        COMMIT @verdict WITH status = 'partial'
    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        COMMIT @pro_history WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```
     | 
     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 9
     | Tokens: 12737 in / 5624 out
     | Latency: 91633ms
     | ------------------------------------------------------------

"Open-sourcing AI development is crucial for ensuring that the technology serves humanity's best interests. By prioritizing transparency, accountability, and collaboration, we can harness the full potential of AI while minimizing its risks."

**Argument:**

1. **Promoting Global Cooperation:** Open-sourcing AI systems facilitates global cooperation and knowledge-sharing among researchers, developers, and policymakers.
2. **Addressing Climate Change and Sustainability:** Democratizing access to AI technology accelerates the development of clean energy sources, reduces carbon emissions, and promotes environmental sustainability.
3. **Enhancing Human Capabilities:** Empowering diverse backgrounds of researchers and developers amplifies human capabilities and enhances our collective potential.
4. **Mitigating Biases and Discrimination:** Identifying and addressing bias in AI decision-making processes ensures that AI systems serve the greater good and promote social justice.
5. **Upholding Democratic Values:** Embedding democratic values such as transparency, accountability, and participation in the development process promotes a future where AI serves humanity's best interests.

**Addressing Counterargument 1: Risk of Security Breaches**
"Implementing robust security measures like encryption and access controls can mitigate potential vulnerabilities."

**Addressing Counterargument 2: Intellectual Property Concerns**
"Robust licensing agreements, intellectual property frameworks, and transparent licensing terms can protect creators' rights while allowing open access to AI source code."

**Addressing Counterargument 3: Lack of Expertise**
"Regular testing, evaluation, and peer review ensure that open-sourced AI systems meet quality standards."

**Addressing Counterargument 4: Unintended Consequences**

"C collaborative efforts between industry leaders, researchers, and policymakers establish standards and best practices for open-sourced AI, reducing commercial disadvantages."
```
     | ------------------------------------------------------------
     | Variables:
     |   @topic = AI should be open-sourced
     |   @max_rounds = 3
     |   @round = 3
     |   @pro_history = **Title:** The Case for Open-Sourcing AI: Unlocking Collective Progress and Transparency
     | 
     | **Opening Statement:**
     | 
     | As we continue to navigate the complexities of artificial intelligence, it's essential that we prioritize the principles of openness, collaboration, and transparency. By making AI open-sourced, we can harness the collective genius of researchers, developers, and enthusiasts worldwide, fostering a vibrant ecosystem that drives innovation and progress.
     | 
     | **Argument 1: Accelerating Research and Development**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI enables the rapid sharing of knowledge, ideas, and code, accelerating research and development in various fields. By making it easier for others to build upon existing work, we can:
     | 
     | * Reduce duplication of effort and save time
     | * Encourage collaboration and knowledge-sharing among experts
     | * Foster a culture of innovation and experimentation
     | 
     | **Argument 2: Promoting Transparency and Trust**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI promotes transparency by making the underlying code and data accessible to everyone. This ensures that:
     | 
     | * The development process is more accountable and trustworthy
     | * Flaws and biases in AI systems can be identified and addressed more quickly
     | * Users are better informed about how their data is being used
     | 
     | **Argument 3: Supporting Democratization of AI**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI makes it possible for a broader range of people to access, contribute to, and benefit from AI research. By:
     | 
     | * Reducing barriers to entry for new developers and researchers
     | * Encouraging community-driven development and feedback
     | * Fostering a more inclusive and diverse AI ecosystem
     | 
     | **Argument 4: Encouraging Responsible AI Development**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI encourages responsible AI development by promoting:
     | 
     | * Clear communication of AI's limitations and potential biases
     | * Active engagement with stakeholders and users to address concerns
     | * Continuous evaluation and improvement of AI systems to ensure they align with societal values.
     | 
     | By open-sourcing AI, we can unlock the full potential of this technology, drive progress, and build a more transparent, accountable, and inclusive community.
     | ---
     | Here's a counterargument to the opening statement:
     | 
     | **Opening Statement:**
     | 
     | "While the idea of open-sourcing AI systems may seem appealing, it is crucial to consider the potential risks and unintended consequences associated with making sensitive technology available to the public. The complexity of AI systems demands expertise and rigorous testing, which cannot be guaranteed by an open-source model. Moreover, the intellectual property rights of creators are at stake, and uncontrolled sharing could stifle innovation."
     | 
     | **Counterargument:**
     | 
     | 1. **Risk of Security Breaches:** Open-sourcing AI systems can lead to increased vulnerability to cyber-attacks and data breaches. By making sensitive code available, developers may inadvertently create a backdoor for malicious actors to exploit.
     | 
     | 2. **Intellectual Property Concerns:** Allowing open access to AI source code raises concerns about intellectual property rights. Creators of AI systems may struggle to protect their work from theft or unauthorized modifications, which could stifle innovation and limit the potential for commercial success.
     | 
     | 3. **Lack of Expertise:** The complexity of AI systems requires specialized expertise, which is not always available in open-source communities. Without proper vetting and testing, open-sourced AI systems may not meet the necessary standards of quality and reliability.
     | 
     | 4. **Unintended Consequences:** Open-sourcing AI systems can lead to unintended consequences, such as the proliferation of biased or flawed code. Without careful review and evaluation, open-source AI systems may perpetuate existing social injustices or create new ones.
     | 
     | 5. **Commercial Disadvantage:** By allowing open access to AI source code, developers may inadvertently disadvantage themselves in the marketplace. Companies that prioritize secrecy and exclusivity over openness may gain a competitive advantage over their rivals.
     | 
     | In conclusion, while the idea of open-sourcing AI systems has its merits, it is essential to consider the potential risks and unintended consequences associated with this approach. We must carefully weigh the benefits against the costs and ensure that any open-source model prioritizes security, intellectual property protection, and responsible innovation.
     | ---
     | Here is a potential response to the task "pro_argument" with an opening statement and argument:
     | 
     | **Opening Statement:**
     | 
     | "While some may argue that keeping AI development under wraps is necessary for commercial success or national security, we must consider the long-term consequences of secrecy and exclusivity. As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it's imperative that we prioritize transparency, accountability, and collaboration in its development. Open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring progress, innovation, and human well-being."
     | 
     | **Argument:**
     | 
     | 1. **Promoting Global Cooperation:** Open-sourcing AI systems can facilitate global cooperation and knowledge-sharing among researchers, developers, and policymakers. By making the code available, we can foster a collaborative environment that transcends national boundaries and promotes peace.
     | 
     | 2. **Addressing Climate Change and Sustainability:** As climate change becomes an increasingly pressing issue, open-sourcing AI systems can help us develop more efficient and sustainable solutions. By democratizing access to AI technology, we can accelerate the development of clean energy sources, reduce carbon emissions, and promote environmental sustainability.
     | 
     | 3. **Enhancing Human Capabilities:** Open-sourced AI systems can amplify human capabilities and enhance our collective potential. By empowering researchers and developers from diverse backgrounds to contribute to AI development, we can create more inclusive and equitable societies that benefit humanity as a whole.
     | 
     | 4. **Mitigating Biases and Discrimination:** Open-sourcing AI systems provides an opportunity for researchers to examine and address bias in AI decision-making processes. By making the code available, developers can identify and mitigate potential biases, ensuring that AI systems serve the greater good and promote social justice.
     | 
     | 5. **Upholding Democratic Values:** As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it's essential that we prioritize democratic values such as transparency, accountability, and participation. Open-sourcing AI systems ensures that these principles are embedded in the development process, promoting a future where AI serves humanity's best interests and reinforces democratic values.
     | 
     | In conclusion, open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring global cooperation, addressing climate change, enhancing human capabilities, mitigating biases, and upholding democratic values. By embracing openness and transparency, we can create a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole and promotes a brighter future for all.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 1: Risk of Security Breaches**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may increase vulnerability to cyber-attacks, this can be mitigated by implementing robust security measures, such as encryption and access controls.
     | * Regular testing and evaluation of open-sourced AI systems can help identify vulnerabilities before they become widespread.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 2: Intellectual Property Concerns**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust licensing agreements and intellectual property frameworks can help protect the rights of creators while still allowing for open access to AI source code.
     | * Allowing for transparent and publicly disclosed licensing terms can also provide clarity for developers and users, reducing the risk of disputes or issues related to IP infringement.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 3: Lack of Expertise**
     | 
     | * While it's true that specialized expertise is required for complex AI systems, this doesn't mean that open-source communities are inherently unqualified.
     | * Regular testing, evaluation, and peer review can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems meet certain standards of quality and reliability.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 4: Unintended Consequences**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust evaluation and testing protocols can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems are thoroughly vetted before they enter the public domain.
     | * Regular monitoring and assessment of open-sourced AI systems can also help identify potential issues or biases before they become widespread.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 5: Commercial Disadvantage**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may inadvertently disadvantage companies that prioritize secrecy and exclusivity, this doesn't mean that open-source models are inherently inferior.
     | * Collaborative efforts between industry leaders, researchers, and policymakers can help establish standards and best practices for open-sourced AI, reducing the risk of commercial disadvantages.
     | 
     | By addressing these counterarguments and emphasizing the benefits of open-sourcing AI systems, it's possible to build a stronger case in favor of this approach.
     | ---
     | Based on the provided arguments and counterarguments, here is a potential response to the task "pro_argument" with an opening statement and argument:
     | 
     | **Opening Statement:**
     | 
     | "As we stand at the threshold of the fourth industrial revolution, it's imperative that we prioritize the principles of openness, transparency, and collaboration in AI development. Open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring accountability, security, and progress. By embracing openness and transparency, we can create a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole and promotes a brighter future for all."
     | 
     | **Argument:**
     | 
     | 1. **Promoting Global Cooperation:** Open-sourcing AI systems can facilitate global cooperation and knowledge-sharing among researchers, developers, and policymakers. By making the code available, we can foster a collaborative environment that transcends national boundaries and promotes peace.
     | 
     | 2. **Addressing Climate Change and Sustainability:** As climate change becomes an increasingly pressing issue, open-sourcing AI systems can help us develop more efficient and sustainable solutions. By democratizing access to AI technology, we can accelerate the development of clean energy sources, reduce carbon emissions, and promote environmental sustainability.
     | 
     | 3. **Enhancing Human Capabilities:** Open-sourced AI systems can amplify human capabilities and enhance our collective potential. By empowering researchers and developers from diverse backgrounds to contribute to AI development, we can create more inclusive and equitable societies that benefit humanity as a whole.
     | 
     | 4. **Mitigating Biases and Discrimination:** Open-sourcing AI systems provides an opportunity for researchers to examine and address bias in AI decision-making processes. By making the code available, developers can identify and mitigate potential biases, ensuring that AI systems serve the greater good and promote social justice.
     | 
     | 5. **Upholding Democratic Values:** As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it's essential that we prioritize democratic values such as transparency, accountability, and participation. Open-sourcing AI systems ensures that these principles are embedded in the development process, promoting a future where AI serves humanity's best interests and reinforces democratic values.
     | 
     | In conclusion, open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring global cooperation, addressing climate change, enhancing human capabilities, mitigating biases, and upholding democratic values. By embracing openness and transparency, we can create a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole and promotes a brighter future for all.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 1: Risk of Security Breaches**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may increase vulnerability to cyber-attacks, this can be mitigated by implementing robust security measures, such as encryption and access controls.
     | * Regular testing and evaluation of open-sourced AI systems can help identify vulnerabilities before they become widespread.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 2: Intellectual Property Concerns**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust licensing agreements and intellectual property frameworks can help protect the rights of creators while still allowing for open access to AI source code.
     | * Allowing for transparent and publicly disclosed licensing terms can also provide clarity for developers and users, reducing the risk of disputes or issues related to IP infringement.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 3: Lack of Expertise**
     | 
     | * While it's true that specialized expertise is required for complex AI systems, this doesn't mean that open-source communities are inherently unqualified.
     | * Regular testing, evaluation, and peer review can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems meet certain standards of quality and reliability.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 4: Unintended Consequences**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust evaluation and testing protocols can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems are thoroughly vetted before they enter the public domain.
     | * Regular monitoring and assessment of open-sourced AI systems can also help identify potential issues or biases before they become widespread.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 5: Commercial Disadvantage**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may inadvertently disadvantage companies that prioritize secrecy and exclusivity, this doesn't mean that open-source models are inherently inferior.
     | * Collaborative efforts between industry leaders, researchers, and policymakers can help establish standards and best practices for open-sourced AI, reducing the risk of commercial disadvantages.
     | 
     | By addressing these counterarguments and emphasizing the benefits of open-sourcing AI systems, it's possible to build a stronger case in favor of this approach.
     |   @con_history = A debate on the topic of "AI should be open-sourced." Here's a possible argument and opening statement:
     | 
     | **Opening Statement:**
     | 
     | "Ladies and gentlemen, today we gather to discuss a pressing issue that has far-reaching implications for the future of artificial intelligence. As AI technology continues to advance at an unprecedented rate, it is imperative that we consider the principles of openness and transparency in its development. Open-sourcing AI systems is not just a moral imperative; it's also a necessary step towards ensuring accountability, security, and progress. By making AI code available for anyone to review, modify, and distribute, we can foster a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole."
     | 
     | **Argument:**
     | 
     | 1. **Promoting Transparency and Accountability:** Open-sourcing AI systems allows developers to scrutinize the code, identify potential biases, and address vulnerabilities before they can be exploited by malicious actors. This transparency promotes accountability and ensures that AI is developed with human values in mind.
     | 
     | 2. **Fostering Collaboration and Innovation:** By providing access to AI source code, researchers and developers from around the world can contribute to the improvement of AI systems. This collaborative approach accelerates innovation, as diverse perspectives and expertise come together to drive progress.
     | 
     | 3. **Enhancing Security and Reliability:** Open-sourcing AI systems enables security experts to review and test the code, identifying potential weaknesses and vulnerabilities before they can be exploited. This proactive approach ensures that AI systems are more reliable and secure, reducing the risk of catastrophic failures.
     | 
     | 4. **Addressing Bias and Fairness:** Open-sourced AI systems provide an opportunity for researchers to examine and address bias in AI decision-making processes. By making the code available, developers can identify and mitigate potential biases, ensuring that AI systems serve the greater good.
     | 
     | 5. **Upholding Human Rights and Values:** As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it is essential that we prioritize human rights and values. Open-sourcing AI systems ensures that these principles are embedded in the development process, promoting a future where AI serves humanity's best interests.
     | 
     | In conclusion, open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring accountability, security, and progress. By embracing openness and transparency, we can create a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole.
     | ---
     | To respond to the counterargument, here are some potential points to consider:
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 1: Risk of Security Breaches**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may increase vulnerability to cyber-attacks, this can be mitigated by implementing robust security measures, such as encryption and access controls.
     | * Regular testing and evaluation of open-sourced AI systems can help identify vulnerabilities before they become widespread.
     | * Collaborative efforts between developers, researchers, and security experts can also help identify and address potential security concerns.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 2: Intellectual Property Concerns**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust licensing agreements and intellectual property frameworks can help protect the rights of creators while still allowing for open access to AI source code.
     | * Allowing for transparent and publicly disclosed licensing terms can also provide clarity for developers and users, reducing the risk of disputes or issues related to IP infringement.
     | * Collaborative efforts between industry leaders, researchers, and policymakers can help establish standards and best practices for IP protection in the context of open-sourced AI.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 3: Lack of Expertise**
     | 
     | * While it's true that specialized expertise is required for complex AI systems, this doesn't mean that open-source communities are inherently unqualified.
     | * Regular testing, evaluation, and peer review can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems meet certain standards of quality and reliability.
     | * Collaborative efforts between developers, researchers, and experts from various fields can also help identify areas where expertise may be lacking and provide solutions.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 4: Unintended Consequences**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust evaluation and testing protocols can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems are thoroughly vetted before they enter the public domain.
     | * Regular monitoring and assessment of open-sourced AI systems can also help identify potential issues or biases before they become widespread.
     | * Collaborative efforts between developers, researchers, and users can also help address concerns related to bias, diversity, and inclusion in AI systems.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 5: Commercial Disadvantage**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may inadvertently disadvantage companies that prioritize secrecy and exclusivity, this doesn't mean that open-source models are inherently inferior.
     | * Collaborative efforts between industry leaders, researchers, and policymakers can help establish standards and best practices for open-sourced AI, reducing the risk of commercial disadvantages.
     | * Open-sourcing AI systems can also provide opportunities for new businesses and entrepreneurs to emerge, creating a more diverse and inclusive ecosystem.
     | 
     | By addressing these counterarguments and emphasizing the benefits of open-sourcing AI systems, it's possible to build a stronger case in favor of this approach.
     | ---

     | 
     | * Implementing robust evaluation and testing protocols can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems are thoroughly vetted before they enter the public domain.

     |

     |   @pro = **Title:** The Case for Open-Sourcing AI: Unlocking Collective Progress and Transparency
     | 
     | **Opening Statement:**
     | 
     | As we continue to navigate the complexities of artificial intelligence, it's essential that we prioritize the principles of openness, collaboration, and transparency. By making AI open-sourced, we can harness the collective genius of researchers, developers, and enthusiasts worldwide, fostering a vibrant ecosystem that drives innovation and progress.
     | 
     | **Argument 1: Accelerating Research and Development**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI enables the rapid sharing of knowledge, ideas, and code, accelerating research and development in various fields. By making it easier for others to build upon existing work, we can:
     | 
     | * Reduce duplication of effort and save time
     | * Encourage collaboration and knowledge-sharing among experts
     | * Foster a culture of innovation and experimentation
     | 
     | **Argument 2: Promoting Transparency and Trust**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI promotes transparency by making the underlying code and data accessible to everyone. This ensures that:
     | 
     | * The development process is more accountable and trustworthy
     | * Flaws and biases in AI systems can be identified and addressed more quickly
     | * Users are better informed about how their data is being used
     | 
     | **Argument 3: Supporting Democratization of AI**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI makes it possible for a broader range of people to access, contribute to, and benefit from AI research. By:
     | 
     | * Reducing barriers to entry for new developers and researchers
     | * Encouraging community-driven development and feedback
     | * Fostering a more inclusive and diverse AI ecosystem
     | 
     | **Argument 4: Encouraging Responsible AI Development**
     | 
     | Open-sourcing AI encourages responsible AI development by promoting:
     | 
     | * Clear communication of AI's limitations and potential biases
     | * Active engagement with stakeholders and users to address concerns
     | * Continuous evaluation and improvement of AI systems to ensure they align with societal values.
     | 
     | By open-sourcing AI, we can unlock the full potential of this technology, drive progress, and build a more transparent, accountable, and inclusive community.

     | **Opening Statement:**

     | "Ladies and gentlemen, today we gather to discuss a pressing issue that has far-reaching implications for the future of artificial intelligence. As AI technology continues to advance at an unprecedented rate, it is imperative that we consider the principles of openness and transparency in its development. Open-sourcing AI systems is not just a moral imperative; it's also a necessary step towards ensuring accountability, security, and progress. By making AI code available for anyone to review, modify, and distribute, we can foster a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole."
     | 
     | **Argument:**
     | 
     | 1. **Promoting Transparency and Accountability:** Open-sourcing AI systems allows developers to scrutinize the code, identify potential biases, and address vulnerabilities before they can be exploited by malicious actors. This transparency promotes accountability and ensures that AI is developed with human values in mind.
     | 
     | 2. **Fostering Collaboration and Innovation:** By providing access to AI source code, researchers and developers from around the world can contribute to the improvement of AI systems. This collaborative approach accelerates innovation, as diverse perspectives and expertise come together to drive progress.
     | 
     | 3. **Enhancing Security and Reliability:** Open-sourcing AI systems enables security experts to review and test the code, identifying potential weaknesses and vulnerabilities before they can be exploited. This proactive approach ensures that AI systems are more reliable and secure, reducing the risk of catastrophic failures.
     | 
     | 4. **Addressing Bias and Fairness:** Open-sourced AI systems provide an opportunity for researchers to examine and address bias in AI decision-making processes. By making the code available, developers can identify and mitigate potential biases, ensuring that AI systems serve the greater good.
     | 
     | 5. **Upholding Human Rights and Values:** As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it is essential that we prioritize human rights and values. Open-sourcing AI systems ensures that these principles are embedded in the development process, promoting a future where AI serves humanity's best interests.
     | 
     | In conclusion, open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring accountability, security, and progress. By embracing openness and transparency, we can create a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole.

Open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring accountability, security, and progress. By embracing openness and transparency, we can create a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole and promotes a brighter future for all."
     | 
     | **Argument:**

By making the code available, we can foster a collaborative environment that transcends national boundaries and promotes peace.
     | 
     | 2. **Addressing Climate Change and Sustainability:** As climate change becomes an increasingly pressing issue, open-sourcing AI systems can help us develop more efficient and sustainable solutions. By democratizing access to AI technology, we can accelerate the development of clean energy sources, reduce carbon emissions, and promote environmental sustainability.
     | 
     | 3. **Enhancing Human Capabilities:** Open-sourced AI systems can amplify human capabilities and enhance our collective potential. By empowering researchers and developers from diverse backgrounds to contribute to AI development, we can create more inclusive and equitable societies that benefit humanity as a whole.
     | 
     | 4. **Mitigating Biases and Discrimination:** Open-sourcing AI systems provides an opportunity for researchers to examine and address bias in AI decision-making processes. By making the code available, developers can identify and mitigate potential biases, ensuring that AI systems serve the greater good and promote social justice.
     | 
     | 5. **Upholding Democratic Values:** As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it's essential that we prioritize democratic values such as transparency, accountability, and participation. Open-sourcing AI systems ensures that these principles are embedded in the development process, promoting a future where AI serves humanity's best interests and reinforces democratic values.
     | 
     | In conclusion, open-sourcing AI systems is not only a moral obligation but also a necessary step towards ensuring global cooperation, addressing climate change, enhancing human capabilities, mitigating biases, and upholding democratic values. By embracing openness and transparency, we can create a collaborative environment that benefits humanity as a whole and promotes a brighter future for all.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 1: Risk of Security Breaches**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may increase vulnerability to cyber-attacks, this can be mitigated by implementing robust security measures, such as encryption and access controls.
     | * Regular testing and evaluation of open-sourced AI systems can help identify vulnerabilities before they become widespread.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 2: Intellectual Property Concerns**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust licensing agreements and intellectual property frameworks can help protect the rights of creators while still allowing for open access to AI source code.
     | * Allowing for transparent and publicly disclosed licensing terms can also provide clarity for developers and users, reducing the risk of disputes or issues related to IP infringement.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 3: Lack of Expertise**
     | 
     | * While it's true that specialized expertise is required for complex AI systems, this doesn't mean that open-source communities are inherently unqualified.
     | * Regular testing, evaluation, and peer review can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems meet certain standards of quality and reliability.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 4: Unintended Consequences**
     | 
     | * Implementing robust evaluation and testing protocols can help ensure that open-sourced AI systems are thoroughly vetted before they enter the public domain.
     | * Regular monitoring and assessment of open-sourced AI systems can also help identify potential issues or biases before they become widespread.
     | 
     | **Addressing Counterargument 5: Commercial Disadvantage**
     | 
     | * While it's true that open-sourcing AI systems may inadvertently disadvantage companies that prioritize secrecy and exclusivity, this doesn't mean that open-source models are inherently inferior.
     | * Collaborative efforts between industry leaders, researchers, and policymakers can help establish standards and best practices for open-sourced AI, reducing the risk of commercial disadvantages.
     | 
     | By addressing these counterarguments and emphasizing the benefits of open-sourcing AI systems, it's possible to build a stronger case in favor of this approach.

```spl
-- Recipe 12: Plan and Execute
-- A planner agent decomposes a task into steps, then an executor implements each one.
-- When output_dir is set, generated code files are written to disk one-by-one.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/12_plan_and_execute/plan_execute.spl --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/12_plan_and_execute/tools.py \
--       task="Build a REST API for a todo app" \
--       output_dir="cookbook/12_plan_and_execute/output"
--
--   spl run cookbook/12_plan_and_execute/plan_execute.spl --adapter ollama \
--       task="Set up a CI/CD pipeline for a Python project"


-- Phase 1: Decompose task into a numbered implementation plan
CREATE FUNCTION plan(task TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a senior software architect. Break down this task into clear implementation steps:

Task: {task}

Output a numbered list of concrete steps (3–6 steps). Each step should be specific
and independently executable. No prose — just the numbered list.
$$;

-- Count how many steps are in the plan (capped at max_steps)
CREATE FUNCTION count_steps(plan TEXT, max_steps TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Count the number of numbered steps in this plan.
Return ONLY a single integer — no explanation, no text.
If there are more than {max_steps} steps, return {max_steps}.

Plan:
{plan}
$$;

-- Extract step N from the plan (0-indexed)
CREATE FUNCTION extract_step(plan TEXT, step_index TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Extract step number {step_index} (0-indexed) from this numbered plan and return
ONLY that step's description. No numbering prefix. No extra text.

Plan:
{plan}
$$;

-- Execute a step: produce a concise design decision + list of files to create
CREATE FUNCTION execute_step(current_step TEXT, prior_results TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a senior software engineer planning an implementation.

Step: {current_step}
Completed so far: {prior_results}

Describe in 2-3 sentences what this step produces and list the filenames it creates.
Be brief — no code yet, just the design decision and file list.
$$;

-- Validate that a step produced meaningful output
CREATE FUNCTION validate_step(current_step TEXT, step_result TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Did the following implementation successfully address the step?

Step: {current_step}
Implementation: {step_result}

Reply with exactly one word: "passed" or "failed".
$$;

-- Re-plan after a step failure
CREATE FUNCTION replan(task TEXT, plan TEXT, step_index TEXT, step_result TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
A step in our implementation plan failed. Create a revised plan.

Original task: {task}
Original plan: {plan}
Failed at step: {step_index}
Failure details: {step_result}

Output a new numbered plan starting from step {step_index}. Keep completed steps as-is.
$$;

-- Phase 4a: List all source files to create (no code — just filenames + one-line descriptions)
CREATE FUNCTION outline_files(task TEXT, results TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a senior software engineer. Based on the implementation plan below, list every
source file that must be created to complete the task.

Task: {task}

Implementation plan:
{results}

Output a numbered list — one file per line — with the filename and a one-sentence description.
Always include a README.md as the last item.
Example:
1. app.py - Flask application entry point, registers blueprints and starts the server
2. models.py - SQLAlchemy ORM models for Todo and User
3. README.md - Setup instructions, project layout, and example API calls

No code. No prose. Just the numbered file list.
$$;

-- Count files in the outline
CREATE FUNCTION count_files(outline TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Count the number of numbered items in this file list.
Return ONLY a single integer — no explanation, no text.

List:
{outline}
$$;

-- Extract one file entry at index N (0-indexed)
CREATE FUNCTION extract_file(outline TEXT, file_index TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Extract item number {file_index} (0-indexed) from this numbered file list and return
ONLY that item's filename and description. No number prefix. No extra text.

List:
{outline}
$$;

-- Generate complete code for ONE file
CREATE FUNCTION generate_file(task TEXT, results TEXT, file_desc TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a senior software engineer. Write complete, runnable code for ONE source file.

Task: {task}

Implementation plan:
{results}

File to create: {file_desc}

Output a SINGLE fenced code block. The FIRST line inside the fence MUST be a filename comment:

```python
# filename: app/main.py
...complete code...
```
     | 
     | Requirements:
     | - Complete, runnable code — no placeholders, no TODOs.
     | - Error handling, type hints, brief inline comments.
     | - Only this one file — nothing else.
     | $$;
     | 
     | -- Summarize what was built
     | CREATE FUNCTION summarize(task TEXT, results TEXT, file_outline TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
     | In 3-5 sentences, describe what was built for this task and how to run it.
     | 
     | Task: {task}
     | Files created:
     | {file_outline}
     | $$;
     | 
     | 
     | WORKFLOW plan_and_execute
     |     INPUT:
     |         @task TEXT DEFAULT 'Build a REST API for a todo app',
     |         @output_dir TEXT DEFAULT '',
     |         @max_steps INTEGER DEFAULT 5
     |     OUTPUT: @final_report TEXT
     | DO
     |     @step_index := 0
     |     @results := ''
     | 
     |     -- Phase 1: Plan
     |     GENERATE plan(@task) INTO @plan
     | 
     |     -- Phase 2: Count steps (capped at max_steps)
     |     GENERATE count_steps(@plan, @max_steps) INTO @step_count
     | 
     |     -- Phase 3: Execute each step (brief design notes only — no code)
     |     WHILE @step_index < @step_count DO
     |         GENERATE extract_step(@plan, @step_index) INTO @current_step
     |         GENERATE execute_step(@current_step, @results) INTO @step_result
     |         GENERATE validate_step(@current_step, @step_result) INTO @validation
     | 
     |         EVALUATE @validation
     |             WHEN 'failed' THEN
     |                 GENERATE replan(@task, @plan, @step_index, @step_result) INTO @plan
     |                 GENERATE count_steps(@plan, @max_steps) INTO @step_count
     |                 @step_index := 0
     |                 @results := ''
     |             OTHERWISE
     |                 @results := @results + '\n## Step ' + @step_index + '\n' + @step_result
     |                 @step_index := @step_index + 1
     |         END
     |     END
     | 
     |     -- Phase 4: Outline all files to generate
     |     GENERATE outline_files(@task, @results) INTO @file_outline
     |     GENERATE count_files(@file_outline) INTO @file_count
     | 
     |     -- Phase 5: Generate each file individually (one LLM call per file — avoids truncation)
     |     @file_index := 0
     |     WHILE @file_index < @file_count DO
     |         GENERATE extract_file(@file_outline, @file_index) INTO @current_file
     |         GENERATE generate_file(@task, @results, @current_file) INTO @file_code
     |         CALL write_code_files(@file_code, @output_dir) INTO @file_written
     |         @file_index := @file_index + 1
     |     END
     | 
     |     -- Phase 6: Summary report
     |     GENERATE summarize(@task, @results, @file_outline) INTO @final_report
     | 
     |     COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'complete', steps_executed = @step_index, files_generated = @file_count
     | 
     | EXCEPTION
     |     WHEN MaxIterationsReached THEN
     |         GENERATE summarize(@task, @results, @file_outline) INTO @final_report
     |         COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'partial', steps_executed = @step_index
     |     WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
     |         COMMIT @results WITH status = 'budget_limit'
     | END
     | ```
     |

For the task of building a REST API for a todo app, a modular architecture is employed consisting of multiple files. The core components include `controllers.py`, `services.py` (optional), `repositories.py` (optional), and `models.py`. 

To run this application, follow these steps:

1. First, install the required libraries by opening your terminal and running `pip install -r requirements.txt`.
2. Initialize a database using SQLAlchemy by navigating to the directory containing the models.py file.
3. Run the application using Python, e.g., `python controllers.py` (if services.py is not needed), or `python main.py` if you've created one.
4. To test the API endpoints, use tools like `curl`, Postman, or any other HTTP client.

Note: The instructions might vary depending on individual project setup and chosen technologies for the database and/or frameworks used for building the application.

     | def create_todo():
     |     try:
     |         data = request.json
     |         if 'title' not in data or 'description' not in data:
     |             raise ValidationError('Missing title or description')
     |         
     |         new_todo = Todo(data['title'], data['description'])
     |         db.session.add(new_todo)
     |         db.session.commit()
     |         return jsonify(TodoSchema().dump(new_todo)), 201
     |     except ValidationError as e:
     |         return jsonify({'error': str(e)}), 400
     |     except Exception as e:
     |         db.session.rollback()
     |         return jsonify({'error': 'Internal server error'}), 500
     |

     | def get_todo(todo_id):
     |     todo = Todo.query.get(todo_id)
     |     if not todo:
     |         return jsonify({'error': 'Todo item not found'}), 404
     |     return jsonify(TodoSchema().dump(todo))
     | 
     | @app.route('/todos/<int:todo_id>', methods=['PUT'])
     | def update_todo(todo_id):
     |     todo = Todo.query.get(todo_id)
     |     if not todo:
     |         return jsonify({'error': 'Todo item not found'}), 404
     |     
     |     try:
     |         data = request.json
     |         if 'title' in data and todo.title != data['title']:
     |             todo.title = data['title']
     |         if 'description' in data and todo.description != data['description']:
     |             todo.description = data['description']
     |         
     |         db.session.commit()
     |         return jsonify(TodoSchema().dump(todo))
     |     except ValidationError as e:
     |         return jsonify({'error': str(e)}), 400
     |     except Exception as e:
     |         db.session.rollback()
     |         return jsonify({'error': 'Internal server error'}), 500
     | 
     | @app.route('/todos/<int:todo_id>', methods=['DELETE'])
     | def delete_todo(todo_id):
     |     todo = Todo.query.get(todo_id)
     |     if not todo:
     |         return jsonify({'error': 'Todo item not found'}), 404
     |     
     |     db.session.delete(todo)
     |     db.session.commit()
     |     return {'message': 'Todo item deleted'}

     |     app.run(debug=True)

```python
import os
from flask import Flask, request, jsonify
from flask_sqlalchemy import SQLAlchemy
from flask_marshmallow import Marshmallow
from marshmallow.exceptions import ValidationError
from werkzeug.security import generate_password_hash, check_password_hash

app = Flask(__name__)

# Database configuration
DATABASE_URL = 'sqlite:///todo.db'
app.config['SQLALCHEMY_DATABASE_URI'] = DATABASE_URL
db = SQLAlchemy(app)
ma = Marshmallow(app)

class Todo(db.Model):
    """Represents a todo item."""
    id = db.Column(db.Integer, primary_key=True)
    title = db.Column(db.String(100), nullable=False)
    description = db.Column(db.Text, nullable=False)
    done = db.Column(db.Boolean, default=False)

    def __init__(self, title: str, description: str):
        """Initializes a new todo item."""
        self.title = title
        self.description = description

class TodoSchema(ma.SQLAlchemyAutoSchema):
    """Serializes and deserializes Todo objects."""
    class Meta:
        model = Todo
        include_fk = True

# Route definitions
@app.route('/todos', methods=['GET'])
def get_all_todos():
    """Returns a list of all todo items."""
    todos = Todo.query.all()
    return jsonify([TodoSchema().dump(todo) for todo in todos])

@app.route('/todos', methods=['POST'])
def create_todo():
    """Creates a new todo item and returns it in the response."""
    try:
        data = request.get_json()
        if not data or ('title' not in data and 'description' not in data):
            raise ValidationError('Missing title or description')
        
        new_todo = Todo(data['title'], data['description'])
        db.session.add(new_todo)
        db.session.commit()
        return jsonify(TodoSchema().dump(new_todo)), 201
    except ValidationError as e:
        return jsonify({'error': str(e)}), 400
    except Exception as e:
        db.session.rollback()
        return jsonify({'error': 'Internal server error'}), 500

@app.route('/todos/<int:todo_id>', methods=['GET'])
def get_todo(todo_id):
    """Returns a todo item by its ID."""
    todo = Todo.query.get(todo_id)
    if not todo:
        return jsonify({'error': 'Todo item not found'}), 404
    return jsonify(TodoSchema().dump(todo))

@app.route('/todos/<int:todo_id>', methods=['PUT'])
def update_todo(todo_id):
    """Updates a todo item and returns it in the response."""
    todo = Todo.query.get(todo_id)
    if not todo:
        return jsonify({'error': 'Todo item not found'}), 404
    
    try:
        data = request.get_json()
        if 'title' in data and todo.title != data['title']:
            todo.title = data['title']
        if 'description' in data and todo.description != data['description']:
            todo.description = data['description']
        
        db.session.commit()
        return jsonify(TodoSchema().dump(todo))
    except ValidationError as e:
        return jsonify({'error': str(e)}), 400
    except Exception as e:
        db.session.rollback()
        return jsonify({'error': 'Internal server error'}), 500

@app.route('/todos/<int:todo_id>', methods=['DELETE'])
def delete_todo(todo_id):
    """Deletes a todo item."""
    todo = Todo.query.get(todo_id)
    if not todo:
        return jsonify({'error': 'Todo item not found'}), 404
    
    db.session.delete(todo)
    db.session.commit()
    return {'message': 'Todo item deleted'}

if __name__ == '__main__':
    app.run(debug=True)

```spl
-- Recipe 13: Map-Reduce Summarizer
-- Splits a large document into chunks, summarizes each chunk (map),
-- then combines all summaries into a final summary (reduce).
-- Demonstrates the map-reduce pattern for handling content beyond context limits.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/13_map_reduce/map_reduce.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 document="$(cat large_doc.txt)"
--   spl run cookbook/13_map_reduce/map_reduce.spl --adapter ollama document="$(cat README.md)" style="bullet points"
--   spl run cookbook/13_map_reduce/map_reduce.spl --adapter ollama document="long text here..." style="executive brief"

WORKFLOW map_reduce_summarizer
    INPUT: @document TEXT, @style TEXT
    OUTPUT: @final_summary TEXT
DO
    @chunk_index := 0
    @summaries := ''

    -- Step 1: Determine how to split the document
    GENERATE chunk_plan(@document) INTO @chunk_count

    -- Step 2: MAP — summarize each chunk independently
    WHILE @chunk_index < @chunk_count DO
        GENERATE extract_chunk(@document, @chunk_index, @chunk_count) INTO @chunk

        GENERATE summarize_chunk(@chunk, @chunk_index) INTO @chunk_summary

        @summaries := @summaries + '\n[Chunk ' + @chunk_index + ']: ' + @chunk_summary
        @chunk_index := @chunk_index + 1
    END

    -- Step 3: REDUCE — combine all chunk summaries into one
    GENERATE reduce_summaries(@summaries, @style) INTO @final_summary

    -- Step 4: Quality check the final summary
    GENERATE quality_score(@final_summary, @document) INTO @score

    EVALUATE @score
        WHEN > 0.7 THEN
            COMMIT @final_summary WITH status = 'complete', chunks = @chunk_count
        OTHERWISE
            GENERATE improve_summary(@final_summary, @summaries) INTO @final_summary
            COMMIT @final_summary WITH status = 'refined', chunks = @chunk_count
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- If document is too large even for chunking, do hierarchical reduction
        GENERATE reduce_summaries(@summaries, @style) INTO @final_summary
        COMMIT @final_summary WITH status = 'partial'
    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        GENERATE reduce_summaries(@summaries, @style) INTO @final_summary
        COMMIT @final_summary WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```

Improved Summary:

Reduce Summaries

The task involves condensing information from two different types of inputs into concise summaries. The first input is a plain text, which may require summarization based on its content. The second input consists of bullet points, which can be summarized by grouping similar items together or extracting key points.

This task requires the ability to analyze and process different types of data, identify relevant information, and present it in a clear and concise manner.

     | ------------------------------------------------------------

```python
import nltk
from nltk.util import ngrams

# Tokenize the input text into individual words or tokens
tokens = nltk.word_tokenize("The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog. This is a test document for map-reduce summarization.")

# Define the maximum length of each chunk (in words)
chunk_length = 5

# Create chunks by splitting the tokens based on the chunk length
chunks = []
for i in range(len(tokens) - chunk_length + 1):
    chunk = ' '.join(tokens[i:i+chunk_length])
    chunks.append(chunk)

print(chunks)

     | 
     | This will create chunks of approximately 5 words each. However, this is a very simple approach and might not give the desired results depending on your specific use case.
     | 
     | Keep in mind that you can also consider other factors like:
     | 
     | *   NLP models for chunking
     | *   Named Entity Recognition (NER) to group names and other important entities together
     | *   Dependency parsing to understand grammatical relationships between tokens
     | 
     | Here is an updated code snippet using NLTK's `ngrams` function, which generates all unique n-grams from the input:
     | 
```python
import nltk
from nltk.util import ngrams

# Tokenize the input text into individual words or tokens
tokens = nltk.word_tokenize("The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog. This is a test document for map-reduce summarization.")

# Define the maximum length of each chunk (in words)
chunk_length = 5

# Create chunks by splitting the tokens based on the chunk length using ngrams
chunks = []
for r in range(1, chunk_length + 1):
    for gram in ngrams(tokens, r):
        chunk = ' '.join(gram)
        if len(chunk.split()) == chunk_length:
            chunks.append(chunk)

# Remove duplicates by converting to a set and then back to list
chunks = list(set(chunks))

print(chunks)
```
     | 
     | This approach will give you more control over the size of your chunks.

     | 
     | * Key phrases: "The quick brown fox", "jumps over", "lazy dog"
     | * Main idea: The sentence is a well-known pangram (a sentence that uses all the letters of the alphabet) and appears to be used as a test case for map-reduce summarization.
     | 
     | Assuming we're evaluating the quality score based on how relevant and informative the bullet points are, I'd rate this input as follows:
     |

     | * Informative value: 7/10 (while providing some insight into map-reduce summarization, the text doesn't offer much in terms of specific information or context)

     | = 6.4 + 4.9

```spl
-- Recipe 14: Multi-Agent Collaboration
-- Specialized agents (Researcher, Analyst, Writer) collaborate on a report.
-- Each agent has a distinct role and passes results to the next.
-- Demonstrates procedural decomposition, CALL-based delegation, and role specialization.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/14_multi_agent/multi_agent.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 topic="Impact of AI on healthcare"
--   spl run cookbook/14_multi_agent/multi_agent.spl --adapter ollama topic="Future of renewable energy"
--   spl run cookbook/14_multi_agent/multi_agent.spl --adapter ollama topic="State of quantum computing in 2025"

-- Agent 1: Researcher — gathers key facts and sources
PROCEDURE researcher(topic TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
DO
    GENERATE research_facts(topic) INTO @facts
    GENERATE identify_key_themes(@facts) INTO @themes
    @result := @facts + '\n\nKey Themes:\n' + @themes
    COMMIT @result
END

-- Agent 2: Analyst — identifies trends, risks, and opportunities
PROCEDURE analyst(research TEXT, topic TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
DO
    GENERATE analyze_trends(research) INTO @trends
    GENERATE assess_risks(research, topic) INTO @risks
    GENERATE find_opportunities(research, topic) INTO @opportunities
    @result := 'Trends:\n' + @trends + '\n\nRisks:\n' + @risks + '\n\nOpportunities:\n' + @opportunities
    COMMIT @result
END

-- Agent 3: Writer — produces polished final report
PROCEDURE writer(research TEXT, analysis TEXT, topic TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
DO
    GENERATE draft_report(topic, research, analysis) INTO @draft
    GENERATE critique(@draft) INTO @feedback
    GENERATE revise_report(@draft, @feedback) INTO @final
    COMMIT @final
END

-- Orchestrator workflow
WORKFLOW multi_agent_report
    INPUT: @topic TEXT
    OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
    -- Delegate to specialized agents
    CALL researcher(@topic) INTO @research
    CALL analyst(@research, @topic) INTO @analysis
    CALL writer(@research, @analysis, @topic) INTO @report

    COMMIT @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        COMMIT @research WITH status = 'partial_research_only'
    WHEN HallucinationDetected THEN
        RETRY WITH temperature = 0.1
END
```
