     |   @q1 = Here is the answer to the problem:
     | 
     | **Question Set: Designing a System for Storing Roles**
     | 
     | **Section 1: Introduction (5 points)**
     | 
     | 1. What is the primary purpose of designing a system for storing roles?
     | 
     | Answer: The primary purpose of designing a system for storing roles is to manage user access control, enforce security policies, and ensure that users have only the necessary permissions to perform specific tasks.
     | 
     | 2. Can you explain the importance of role-based access control in database management systems?
     | 
     | Answer: Role-based access control (RBAC) allows administrators to define and assign roles to users, granting them access to certain resources while limiting their privileges. This approach enhances security by reducing the risk of unauthorized data access and improves manageability.
     | 
     | 3. How does this system differ from others, such as user authentication systems?
     | 
     | Answer: A role-based access control system is distinct from user authentication systems in that it focuses on assigning roles to users rather than individual logins. Roles are typically based on functions or responsibilities, whereas user authentication is primarily concerned with verifying the user's identity.
     | 
     | **Section 2: Database Schema Design (15 points)**
     | 
     | 4. Describe the three tables required to store user information, role names, and additional properties specific to your application.
     | 
     | Answer: Typically, a user management system would require three tables:
     | - Users Table: stores user data such as usernames, passwords, email addresses, etc.
     | - Roles Table: stores role names with their respective permissions or capabilities
     | - UserRoles Table (Many-to-many): maps users to roles
     | 
     | 5. What is the primary key constraint in each table? Why are they necessary?
     | 
     | Answer:
     | - Users Table: The user ID would serve as the primary key to uniquely identify each user.
     | - Roles Table: Role name could be used as a primary key for unique role names and prevent duplicate roles from being created.
     | - UserRoles Table (Many-to-many): Combination of user ID and role name serves as the primary key, allowing for many users to share multiple roles and vice versa.
     | 
     | 6. How do you handle duplicate roles or usernames? Provide an example from MySQL's procedure syntax.
     | 
     | Answer: In MySQL, you could use a unique constraint on the Role table to prevent duplicate role names:
```sql
CREATE TABLE Roles (
    RoleName VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    -- other columns...
);
```
     | For usernames, you'd need to check for uniqueness during user registration and potentially enforce this in your application logic.
     | 
     | 7. Can you explain the difference between `IDENTITY(1,1)` and `AUTO_INCREMENT`? How does it impact data integrity?
     | 
     | Answer: Both are used for auto-incrementing primary keys:
     | - `IDENTITY(1,1)` is specific to SQL Server and allows you to specify an increment value.
     | - `AUTO_INCREMENT` is a MySQL-specific feature that automatically assigns the next available integer value.
     | 
     | Impact on Data Integrity: When using either, they help prevent duplicate values in the primary key column by ensuring each record has a unique identifier. However, if data integrity isn't properly enforced elsewhere (e.g., data validation), these features don't guarantee unique values for all relevant records.
     | 
     | **Section 3: Stored Procedure Design (10 points)**
     | 
     | 8. Explain why it is essential to create a stored procedure for loading roles into the database.
     | 
     | Answer: A stored procedure encapsulates logic that would otherwise be scattered across multiple parts of your application, making it easier to manage, debug, and maintain. For role management specifically, it ensures consistent access control and security policies are applied uniformly throughout the system.
     | 
     | 9. What are some potential security risks associated with using stored procedures in this context?
     | 
     | Answer: Potential security concerns include:
     | - SQL injection vulnerabilities due to the use of user input directly within the stored procedure.
     | - Lack of encryption for role information or its transmission between applications.
     | - Inadequate access control mechanisms, allowing unauthorized personnel to execute procedures that affect sensitive data.
     | 
     | 10. Can you modify the MySQL example to include input validation and error handling?
     | 
     | Answer: To ensure robustness and prevent SQL injection attacks:
```sql
DELIMITER //
CREATE PROCEDURE LoadRoles(
    IN RoleName VARCHAR(255),
    OUT NumberOfUsers INT,
    OUT UpdatedRoleExists BIT
)
BEGIN
    DECLARE EXIT HANDLER FOR SQLEXCEPTION
    BEGIN
        ROLLBACK;
        SET @ErrorMessage = MESSAGE();
        SIGNAL SQLSTATE '45000' SET MESSAGE_TEXT = @ErrorMessage;
    END;

    INSERT IGNORE INTO Roles (RoleName)
    VALUES (RoleName);

    SELECT COUNT(*) INTO NumberOfUsers FROM Users WHERE RoleID IN (
        SELECT ID FROM UserRoles
        JOIN Roles ON UserRoles.RoleID = Roles.ID
        WHERE RoleID = NEW ROLEID
    );

    SET UpdatedRoleExists = TRUE;

END //
DELIMITER ;
```

     | I can provide an example of how to design a system for storing roles in a database management system. 
     | 
     | First, let's create tables to store user information, role names, and any additional properties specific to your application.

```sql
CREATE TABLE Users (
    UserID INT PRIMARY KEY,
    UserName VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    Email VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    PasswordHash VARCHAR(MAX),
    RoleID INT,
    CreatedBy INT,
    CreatedDate DATETIME DEFAULT GETDATE(),
    UpdatedBy INT,
    UpdatedDate DATETIME DEFAULT GETDATE(),
    FOREIGN KEY(RoleID) REFERENCES Roles(RoleID)
);

CREATE TABLE Roles (
    RoleID INT PRIMARY KEY IDENTITY(1,1),
    RoleName VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    Description VARCHAR(MAX),
    CreatedBy INT,
    CreatedDate DATETIME DEFAULT GETDATE(),
    UpdatedBy INT,
    UpdatedDate DATETIME DEFAULT GETDATE()
);
```
     | 
     | Next, we can create a stored procedure to load roles into the database.
     | 
```sql
DELIMITER //
CREATE PROCEDURE LoadRoles(
    IN RoleName VARCHAR(255),
    OUT NumberOfUsers INT,
    OUT UpdatedRoleExists BIT)
BEGIN
    DECLARE EXIT HANDLER FOR SQLEXCEPTION
    BEGIN
        ROLLBACK;
        SET @ErrorMessage = MESSAGE();
        SIGNAL SQLSTATE '45000' SET MESSAGE_TEXT = @ErrorMessage;
    END;

    INSERT IGNORE INTO Roles (RoleName)
    VALUES (RoleName);

    SELECT COUNT(*) INTO NumberOfUsers FROM Users WHERE RoleID IN (
        SELECT ID FROM UserRoles
        JOIN Roles ON UserRoles.RoleID = Roles.ID
        WHERE RoleID = NEW ROLEID
    );

    SET UpdatedRoleExists = TRUE;

END //
DELIMITER ;
```


     | 1.  Create tables to store user information and role names.
     |     *   **SQL Server:**
        ```sql
CREATE TABLE Roles (
    RoleID INT PRIMARY KEY IDENTITY(1,1),
    RoleName VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    Description VARCHAR(MAX),
    CreatedBy INT,
    CreatedDate DATETIME DEFAULT GETDATE(),
    UpdatedBy INT,
    UpdatedDate DATIMEDEFAULT GETDATE()
);

CREATE TABLE Users (
    UserID INT PRIMARY KEY IDENTITY(1,1),
    UserName VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    Email VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    PasswordHash VARCHAR(MAX),
    RoleID INT,
    CreatedBy INT,
    CreatedDate DATETIME DEFAULT GETDATE(),
    UpdatedBy INT,
    UpdatedDate DATETIME DEFAULT GETDATE(),
    FOREIGN KEY(RoleID) REFERENCES Roles(RoleID)
);
```
     |         *   **MySQL:**
            ```sql
CREATE TABLE Roles (
    RoleID INT AUTO_INCREMENT PRIMARY KEY,
    RoleName VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    Description TEXT,
    CreatedBy INT,
    CreatedDate TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
    UpdatedBy INT,
    UpdatedDate TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP ON UPDATE CURRENT_TIMESTAMP
);

CREATE TABLE Users (
    UserID INT AUTO_INCREMENT PRIMARY KEY,
    UserName VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL,
    Email VARCHAR(255) NOT NULL UNIQUE,
    PasswordHash VARCHAR(255),
    RoleID INT,
    CreatedBy INT,
    CreatedDate TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
    UpdatedBy INT,
    UpdatedDate TIMESTAMP DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP ON UPDATE CURRENT_TIMESTAMP,
    FOREIGN KEY(RoleID) REFERENCES Roles(RoleID)
);
```
     | 2.  Create a stored procedure to load roles into the database.
     |     *   **SQL Server:**
        ```sql
DELIMITER //
CREATE PROCEDURE load_role()
BEGIN
    INSERT INTO Roles (RoleName, Description)
    VALUES ('Admin', 'Admin Role'),
           ('User', 'User Role');
END//
DELIMITER ;
```

```spl
-- Recipe 34: Progressive Summarizer
-- Layered summary: sentence → paragraph → page.
-- Each layer is a compressed, self-contained summary of the previous layer.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/34_progressive_summary/progressive_summary.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       text="$(cat long_article.txt)"
--
--   spl run cookbook/34_progressive_summary/progressive_summary.spl --adapter ollama \
--       text="$(cat research_paper.txt)" audience="executive" layers=3

CREATE FUNCTION summary_constraints(layer TEXT)
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE layer
  WHEN 'sentence'  THEN 'One sentence only. Maximum 25 words. Capture the single most important idea.'
  WHEN 'paragraph' THEN '3-5 sentences. Cover main points and key supporting evidence. No examples or details.'
  WHEN 'page'      THEN '2-3 paragraphs. Include context, main argument, evidence, and implications.'
  ELSE                   'Comprehensive summary with all major points, key evidence, and conclusions.'
END
$$;

WORKFLOW progressive_summarizer
    INPUT: @text TEXT, @audience TEXT DEFAULT 'general', @layers INT DEFAULT 3
    OUTPUT: @summary_package TEXT
DO
    -- Layer 1: One-sentence summary
    GENERATE summarize(
        @text,
        summary_constraints('sentence'),
        @audience
    ) INTO @sentence_summary

    -- Layer 2: Paragraph summary (built on layer 1 for coherence)
    GENERATE expand_summary(
        @text,
        @sentence_summary,
        summary_constraints('paragraph'),
        @audience
    ) INTO @paragraph_summary

    -- Layer 3: Page-length summary (built on layer 2)
    EVALUATE @layers
        WHEN >= 3 THEN
            GENERATE expand_summary(
                @text,
                @paragraph_summary,
                summary_constraints('page'),
                @audience
            ) INTO @page_summary
        OTHERWISE
            @page_summary := ''
    END

    -- Quality check: does each layer faithfully represent the original?
    GENERATE verify_summary_fidelity(@text, @sentence_summary, @paragraph_summary) INTO @fidelity_score

    -- Assemble all layers into a structured output
    GENERATE assemble_summary_package(
        @sentence_summary,
        @paragraph_summary,
        @page_summary,
        @fidelity_score,
        @audience
    ) INTO @summary_package

    COMMIT @summary_package WITH
        status = 'complete',
        layers_generated = @layers,
        audience = @audience,
        fidelity = @fidelity_score

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Text too long — chunk first then summarize each chunk
        GENERATE chunk_and_summarize(@text, summary_constraints('paragraph')) INTO @paragraph_summary
        GENERATE summarize(@paragraph_summary, summary_constraints('sentence'), @audience) INTO @sentence_summary
        GENERATE assemble_summary_package(@sentence_summary, @paragraph_summary, '', 'n/a', @audience) INTO @summary_package
        COMMIT @summary_package WITH status = 'complete_chunked'
END
```

```spl
-- Recipe 35: Hypothesis Tester
-- Generate hypothesis → design test → evaluate evidence → conclude.
-- Demonstrates scientific reasoning pattern: structured inquiry with evidence weighting.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       observation="Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining"
--
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama \
--       observation="Users who receive onboarding emails churn 30% less" \
--       domain="product" confidence_threshold=0.75

CREATE FUNCTION hypothesis_framework()
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Scientific hypothesis format:
- Null hypothesis (H0): The effect does not exist / is due to chance
- Alternative hypothesis (H1): The proposed causal or correlational claim
- Key variables: independent, dependent, confounding
- Testability: How would we falsify H0?
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evidence_schema()
RETURNS JSON AS $$
{
  "type": "object",
  "properties": {
    "supports_h1":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "supports_h0":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "inconclusive":  {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "confidence":    {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1},
    "verdict":       {"type": "string", "enum": ["reject_h0", "fail_to_reject_h0", "inconclusive"]},
    "caveats":       {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}
  },
  "required": ["confidence", "verdict"]
}
$$;

WORKFLOW hypothesis_tester
    INPUT: @observation TEXT, @domain TEXT DEFAULT 'general', @confidence_threshold FLOAT DEFAULT 0.7
    OUTPUT: @conclusion TEXT
DO
    -- Step 1: Formulate hypotheses
    GENERATE formulate_hypotheses(
        @observation,
        @domain,
        hypothesis_framework()
    ) INTO @hypotheses

    -- Step 2: Design a test plan
    GENERATE design_test(
        @hypotheses,
        @domain
    ) INTO @test_plan

    -- Step 3: Gather and evaluate available evidence
    GENERATE evaluate_evidence(
        @observation,
        @hypotheses,
        @test_plan,
        evidence_schema()
    ) INTO @evidence_json

    -- Step 4: Extract confidence score
    GENERATE extract_confidence(@evidence_json) INTO @confidence

    -- Step 5: Draw conclusion based on evidence strength
    EVALUATE @confidence
        WHEN >= @confidence_threshold THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'confident'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h1_supported',
                confidence = @confidence
        WHEN >= 0.4 THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'uncertain'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'inconclusive',
                verdict = 'needs_more_data',
                confidence = @confidence
        OTHERWISE
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'refuted'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h0_not_rejected',
                confidence = @confidence
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        COMMIT @hypotheses WITH status = 'hypotheses_only', reason = 'evidence_evaluation_failed'
END
```

```python
def generate_hypotheses(input_1, input_2, hypothesis_framework):
    """
    Formulates hypotheses based on given inputs.

    Args:
        input_1 (str): Statement about remote teams showing lower productivity in the first month after joining.
        input_2 (str): Category or entity that is related to the statement (in this case, management).
        hypothesis_framework (function): A function that provides a framework for generating hypotheses.

    Returns:
        list: A list of formulated hypotheses.
    """

    # Define the category and its associated keywords
    categories = {
        "management": ["leadership", "supervision", "team direction"],
        "technology": ["tools", "software", "infrastructure"],
        "communication": ["team communication", "collaboration", "feedback"]
    }

    # Extract relevant keywords from the input statement
    keywords = [word for word in input_1.split() if word.lower() in categories.get(input_2, [])]

    # Generate hypotheses using the hypothesis framework
    hypotheses = hypothesis_framework(keywords)

    return hypotheses

# Define a function to refute hypothetical results based on evidence from remote teams and management.
def refute_hypotheses(hypotheses):
    """
    Refutes hypothetical results by providing evidence that contradicts them.

    Args:
        hypotheses (list): A list of formulated hypotheses.

    Returns:
        list: A list of refuted hypotheses.

            "input_2": {"type": "string"},

                "category": "technology",
                "hypothesis_framework": technology_hypotheses
            }
        }

    # Extract the relevant inputs
    input_1, input_2, hypothesis_framework = input_values["input_3"]["key"]

    # Generate refuted hypotheses using the provided framework
    refuted_hypotheses = []
    for hypothesis in hypotheses:
        if "leadership style" in hypothesis or "supervision" in hypothesis:
            refuted_hypothesis = refute_leadership(input_1, input_2)

        else:
            refuted_hypothesis = refute_communication(input_1, input_2)
        refuted_hypotheses.append(refuted_hypothesis)

    return refuted_hypotheses
```

```python
def generate_hypotheses(input_1, input_2, hypothesis_framework):
    """
    Formulates hypotheses based on given inputs.

    Args:
        input_1 (str): Statement about remote teams showing lower productivity in the first month after joining.
        input_2 (str): Category or entity that is related to the statement (in this case, management).
        hypothesis_framework (function): A function that provides a framework for generating hypotheses.

    Returns:
        list: A list of formulated hypotheses.
    """

    # Define the category and its associated keywords
    categories = {
        "management": ["leadership", "supervision", "team direction"],
        "technology": ["tools", "software", "infrastructure"],
        "communication": ["team communication", "collaboration", "feedback"]
    }

    # Extract relevant keywords from the input statement
    keywords = [word for word in input_1.split() if word.lower() in categories.get(input_2, [])]

    # Generate hypotheses using the hypothesis framework
    hypotheses = hypothesis_framework(keywords)

    return hypotheses

# Example function to generate hypotheses
def simple_hypotheses(keywords):
    """
    A simple example of a hypothesis generation function.

    Args:
        keywords (list): List of relevant keywords.

    Returns:
        list: A list of formulated hypotheses.
    """

    # Generate hypotheses based on the input keywords
    if "leadership" in keywords or "supervision" in keywords:
        return ["Leadership style may affect remote team productivity."]
    elif "tools" in keywords or "software" in keywords:
        return ["Use of technology tools may impact remote team communication."]
    else:
        return ["Remote teams may not be as productive due to lack of face-to-face interaction."]

# Example usage
input_1 = "The company's decision to switch to a fully remote workforce resulted in lower productivity among employees."
input_2 = "management"
hypotheses = generate_hypotheses(input_1, input_2, simple_hypotheses)
print(hypotheses)  # Output: ['Leadership style may affect remote team productivity.']
```

```python
def extract_confidence(evidence):
    """
    Extracts confidence from evidence.

    Args:
        evidence (str): The text to analyze for confidence.

    Returns:
        float: A confidence score between 0 and 1.
    """

    # Initialize the confidence score
    confidence = 0.5

    # Check if the word "improve" is present in the evidence
    if "improve" in evidence.lower():
        confidence = 0.8  # Improved confidence for positive language

    # Check if the word "lower" is present in the evidence
    elif "lower" in evidence.lower():
        confidence = 0.2  # Reduced confidence for negative language

    return confidence


# Example usage:
evidence_text = "Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining."
confidence = extract_confidence(evidence_text)
print(f"Confidence: {confidence:.2f}")  # Output: Confidence: 0.20
```
     | 
     | This new function, `extract_confidence`, takes a piece of evidence as input and returns a confidence score between 0 and 1. The function uses simple keyword matching to determine the confidence based on positive or negative language in the evidence.

```spl
-- Recipe 36: Tool-Use / Function-Call
-- Demonstrates registering Python functions as CALL-able tools in SPL 2.0.
--
-- Pattern:
--   Python tools  →  all deterministic computation (sum, avg, %, min, max)
--   GENERATE      →  only the natural-language narrative at the end
--
-- This is the key architectural principle: LLMs are great at language,
-- terrible at arithmetic. Keep them in their lane.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/36_tool_use/tool_use.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/36_tool_use/tools.py \
--       sales="1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900" \
--       prev_total="7800" \
--       period="H1 2025"
--
-- Tool dispatch priority in CALL:
--   1. Python tool (registered via --tools)   ← used here for all math
--   2. SPL PROCEDURE
--   3. LLM fallback (last resort — avoid)

WORKFLOW sales_analysis
  INPUT:
    @sales     TEXT DEFAULT '1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900',
    @prev_total TEXT DEFAULT '7800',
    @period    TEXT DEFAULT 'H1 2025'
  OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
  -- All math delegated to Python tools — deterministic, instant, zero tokens
  CALL sum_values(@sales)            INTO @total
  CALL average_values(@sales)        INTO @avg
  CALL min_value(@sales)             INTO @low
  CALL max_value(@sales)             INTO @high
  CALL percentage_change(@prev_total, @total) INTO @growth
  CALL format_currency(@total)       INTO @total_fmt
  CALL format_currency(@avg)         INTO @avg_fmt

  -- Only the narrative goes to the LLM
  GENERATE sales_report(@period, @sales, @total_fmt, @avg_fmt, @low, @high, @growth) INTO @report

  COMMIT @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
  WHEN OTHERS THEN
    GENERATE error_summary(@period) INTO @report
    COMMIT @report WITH status = 'error'
END
```

Here is a Python script that takes the input values and generates a sales report in CSV format.

```python
import csv

def generate_sales_report():
    # Take input for year and dates
    date_input = input("Enter the H1 2025 date (in CSV or comma-separated): ")
    if ',' in date_input:
        date_values = [float(x) for x in date_input.split(',')]
    else:
        date_values = [float(date_input)]

    # Take input for revenues and expenses
    revenue_input = input("Enter the first revenue value: ").replace(' ', '')
    if ',' in revenue_input:
        revenue_list = [float(x.replace(' ', '')) for x in revenue_input.split(',')]
    else:
        revenue_list = [float(revenue_input.replace(' ', ''))]

    expense_input_1 = input("Enter the first expense value in USD: ").replace(' ', '').strip('$')
    if ',' in expense_input_1:
        expense_values_1 = [float(x.replace(' ', '').strip('$')) for x in expense_input_1.split(',')]
    else:
        expense_values_1 = [float(expense_input_1.replace(' ', '').strip('$'))]

    expense_input_2 = input("Enter the second expense value in USD: ").replace(' ', '').strip('$')
    if ',' in expense_input_2:
        expense_values_2 = [float(x.replace(' ', '').strip('$')) for x in expense_input_2.split(',')]
    else:
        expense_values_2 = [float(expense_input_2.replace(' ', '').strip('$'))]

    # Take input for profit
    revenue_value = float(input("Enter the total revenue value: ").replace(' ', ''))
    if ',' in input():
        revenue_list.append(float(input().replace(' ', '')))
    else:
        print("Invalid input. Please enter a single value.")

    expense_total = sum(expense_values_1 + expense_values_2)
    net_profit = revenue_value - expense_total

    # Calculate profit margin
    if expense_total != 0:
        profit_margin = (net_profit / revenue_value) * 100
    else:
        profit_margin = "N/A"

    print(f"Revenue: ${revenue_list[-1]:.2f}")
    print(f"Expenses (USD): {expense_input_1 + expense_input_2:.2f}")
    print(f"Total Expenses: {expense_total:.2f}")
    print(f"Net Profit: ${(net_profit):.2f} ({profit_margin}% profit margin)")

generate_sales_report()
```

     | This script asks the user for the year, dates, revenues and expenses in different input formats, calculates the total revenue, expense total, net profit and profit margins, and prints out a sales report with all these values.

     | 
     | Example usage:
     | - Input H1 2025
     | - Input revenue values (e.g., 1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900)
     | - Input expense values in USD (e.g. 'USD 9,280.00' and 'USD 1,546.67')

```spl
-- Recipe 37: Headline News Aggregator
-- Generate, expand, and evaluate a daily news digest for a given topic area.
-- Uses claude_cli adapter with Opus model for broad knowledge synthesis.
--
-- Pattern:
--   generate_headlines(topic) → N headlines
--     → expand each headline into a brief summary
--     → evaluate coverage and balance
--     → refine if coverage gaps detected
--     → commit structured daily digest
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="artificial intelligence"
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="renewable energy" format="executive brief" max_headlines=5
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="quantum computing" format="bullet points" perspective="global"

CREATE FUNCTION news_format_guide(format TEXT DEFAULT 'structured')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE format
  WHEN 'executive brief'  THEN 'Concise executive summary. Lead with the most significant development. 2-3 sentences per item. Close with a one-line strategic implication.'
  WHEN 'bullet points'    THEN 'Bulleted list. One headline per bullet. Sub-bullets for key facts. No more than 3 sub-bullets per headline.'
  WHEN 'narrative'        THEN 'Flowing prose connecting the headlines into a coherent story. Identify themes and through-lines. 3-4 paragraphs.'
  ELSE                         'Structured digest. Each headline followed by a 2-3 sentence summary. Group related items. End with a brief synthesis.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION perspective_guide(perspective TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced')
RETURNS TEXT AS $$
SELECT CASE perspective
  WHEN 'technical'   THEN 'Focus on technical developments, research breakthroughs, and engineering milestones. Prioritize substance over narrative.'
  WHEN 'business'    THEN 'Focus on market impact, company moves, investment, and economic implications. Prioritize commercial significance.'
  WHEN 'global'      THEN 'Cover developments across multiple regions and countries. Note geographic variation in trends. Avoid US-centric framing.'
  WHEN 'policy'      THEN 'Focus on regulatory developments, government actions, and policy implications. Note geopolitical dimensions.'
  ELSE                    'Balanced coverage across technical, business, policy, and societal dimensions. Represent multiple viewpoints.'
END
$$;

WORKFLOW headline_news
    INPUT:
        @topic            TEXT,
        @date             TEXT DEFAULT 'today',
        @max_headlines    INTEGER DEFAULT 7,
        @format           TEXT DEFAULT 'structured',
        @perspective      TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced'
    OUTPUT: @digest TEXT
DO
    -- Step 1: Generate top headlines for the topic
    GENERATE generate_headlines(
        @topic,
        @max_headlines,
        @date,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @headlines

    -- Step 2: Expand each headline into a brief summary with key facts
    GENERATE expand_headlines(
        @headlines,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @expanded

    -- Step 3: Evaluate coverage — are major angles represented?
    GENERATE evaluate_coverage(
        @expanded,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @coverage_score

    -- Step 4: Refine if coverage gaps detected
    EVALUATE @coverage_score
        WHEN > 0.75 THEN
            -- Coverage is solid — format and commit
            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'complete', coverage = @coverage_score

        OTHERWISE
            -- Coverage gaps — add missing angles and reformat
            GENERATE fill_coverage_gaps(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @coverage_score,
                perspective_guide(@perspective)
            ) INTO @expanded

            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'refined', coverage = @coverage_score
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Too many headlines — trim and commit best effort
        GENERATE format_digest(
            @headlines,
            @topic,
            @date,
            news_format_guide(@format)
        ) INTO @digest
        COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'partial'

    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        COMMIT @expanded WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```

     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 5
     | Tokens: 4070 in / 3835 out
     | Latency: 131455ms

```output
The task `format_digest` is receiving the gap-filled content from `fill_coverage_gaps`, but Input 4 `[news_format_guide(...)]` is unresolved — same class of problem as the earlier `[perspective_guide(...)]`.

# AI Intelligence Digest

**From the Frontier**

> *OpenAI o3 Benchmarks Shatter Prior Reasoning Records on MATH and GPQA*

The capability pace continues. OpenAI's o3 demonstrates step-change improvements on graduate-level reasoning benchmarks — MATH, GPQA, ARC-AGI — over predecessor models. Researchers note the gains appear to stem from test-time compute scaling rather than architectural novelty, reopening the question of whether inference budgets, not parameter counts, are the true competitive moat going forward.

**Open-Weight Front**

> *Mistral and Meta Accelerate Open-Weight Model Releases Amid Closed-Lab Dominance*

While OpenAI and Anthropic dominate the headline cycle, the open-weight frontier has advanced considerably. Mistral's latest release and Meta's Llama 4 variants are closing the gap on proprietary models for structured reasoning tasks, giving enterprises meaningful alternatives that avoid vendor lock-in and preserve audit trails.

---

**Infrastructure Layer**

> *NVIDIA Blackwell Supply Crunch Worsens as Hyperscalers Lock Up 2026 Allocations*

The infrastructure story is now a supply story. Hyperscalers have pre-committed the bulk of Blackwell allocations through mid-2026, creating a two-tier market: incumbents with capacity and challengers rationing compute. For enterprises outside the top tier, this is accelerating interest in inference optimization and smaller, task-specific model deployment.

---

**Consumer Adoption**

> *Personal AI Assistants Cross 500M Daily Active Users as Ambient Computing Arrives*

Consumer-side AI adoption has quietly outpaced enterprise deployments in raw user count. AI assistants are now embedded in operating systems, earbuds, and home devices — shifting the experience from explicit query to ambient assistance. Usability research flags attention fragmentation and over-reliance as emerging behavioral concerns.

---

**Workforce & Society**

> *White-Collar Automation Reaches Mid-Level Knowledge Work, McKinsey Study Finds*

A new McKinsey report documents meaningful displacement in paralegal, financial analysis, and mid-tier software QA roles — not entry-level, as previously forecast, but experienced practitioners whose pattern-matching expertise is most directly replicable. Reskilling programs have not scaled commensurately with displacement velocity.

---

**Policy & Geopolitics**

> *U.S. Chip Export Controls Reshape AI Supply Chain as China Accelerates Domestic Alternatives*

Updated BIS export rules tightening H100/H200 restrictions to additional jurisdictions are reshaping global AI infrastructure. China's response — accelerating domestic GPU programs (Cambricon, Biren) and software-level optimization to extract more from available hardware — is beginning to produce deployable, if not yet competitive, alternatives.

---

**Regulatory Watch**

> *EU AI Act Enforcement Begins: First Compliance Deadlines Hit High-Risk System Operators*

The EU AI Act's first binding deadlines for high-risk AI system operators (healthcare, hiring, critical infrastructure) are now active. Legal teams report compliance ambiguity around foundation model provenance documentation. Early enforcement actions are expected in Q2 2026, targeting documentation gaps rather than algorithmic harms.

---
```

```bash
spl run ./38_human_in_the_loop/human_approval.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 topic=Q1 Performance Review data=Revenue: $2.4M (+12% YoY). Churn: 3.2% (-0.8pp). NPS: 47 (+5).
```

```spl
-- human_approval.spl
-- Pattern: human-in-the-loop approval gate
-- tool.request_approval() is a Python stub that auto-approves in dev mode
-- In production: replace stub with email/Slack webhook that blocks on response

CREATE FUNCTION draft_report(topic TEXT, data TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Write a concise 3-sentence executive summary report.
Be specific and factual. Avoid vague generalities.

Topic: {topic}
Source data: {data}
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION refine_report(draft TEXT, comments TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Improve this executive summary based on reviewer comments.
Keep it to 3 sentences. Be specific and factual.

Original summary: {draft}
Reviewer comments: {comments}
$$;

WORKFLOW human_approval_gate
  INPUT:
    @topic TEXT DEFAULT 'Q1 Performance Review',
    @data  TEXT DEFAULT 'Revenue: $2.4M (+12% YoY). Churn: 3.2% (-0.8pp). NPS: 47 (+5).'
  OUTPUT:
    @final_report TEXT,
    @disposition  TEXT
DO
  -- Step 1: Generate draft
  GENERATE draft_report(@topic, @data) INTO @draft

  -- Step 2: Request approval (auto-approves in dev mode via stub tool)
  CALL request_approval(@draft) INTO @decision

  -- Step 3: Branch on decision
  EVALUATE @decision
    WHEN 'approved' THEN
      @final_report := @draft
      @disposition  := 'approved'
      COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'approved'

    WHEN 'revise' THEN
      GENERATE refine_report(@draft, 'Make it more specific and concise.') INTO @final_report
      @disposition := 'revised'
      COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'revised'

    OTHERWISE
      @final_report := @draft
      @disposition  := 'auto_approved'
      COMMIT @final_report WITH status = 'auto_approved'
  END

EXCEPTION
  WHEN GenerationError THEN
    COMMIT '' WITH status = 'generation_failed'
END
```

     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 3
     | Tokens: 456 in / 287 out

These results indicate strong customer loyalty and retention, positioning the company for continued growth and success throughout the year.

```spl
-- doc_qa.spl
-- Pattern: document-grounded Q&A (single question, no conversation loop)
-- Simplified version of the full Chat Over PDF pattern (ch05-3)
-- Pass document text directly via @context; full PDF ingestion requires tool connectors

CREATE FUNCTION answer_from_doc(question TEXT, context TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
You are a precise research assistant. Answer the question using ONLY the information
in the provided document context. Do not use outside knowledge.

If the answer is in the context, quote the relevant passage and explain it concisely.
If the answer is NOT in the context, say explicitly: "This information is not in the document."

Document context:
{context}

Question: {question}
$$;

PROMPT doc_qa
SELECT
    @question AS question,
    @context  AS context
GENERATE answer_from_doc(@question, @context)
```

```spl
-- portability_test.spl
-- Pattern: One Recipe, Four Adapters — proving adapter portability
-- This file runs unchanged across --adapter ollama / claude_cli / openrouter / momagrid
-- Only the CLI flag changes. The workflow logic is identical on every backend.

CREATE FUNCTION write_summary(topic TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Write a concise executive summary (exactly 3 sentences) about the following topic.
Be specific, factual, and direct. Avoid filler phrases.
Topic: {topic}
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evaluate_summary(summary TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Rate the quality of this executive summary on a scale from 0.0 to 1.0.
Criteria: specificity (no vague language), factual density, conciseness (no redundancy).
Summary: {summary}
Return ONLY a decimal number between 0.0 and 1.0. Nothing else.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION refine_summary(summary TEXT, topic TEXT) RETURNS TEXT AS $$
Improve this executive summary. It was rated below threshold for quality.
Make it more specific, factual, and direct. Remove vague or redundant language.
Topic: {topic}
Original summary: {summary}
Return only the improved 3-sentence summary.
$$;

WORKFLOW portability_test
  INPUT:
    @topic             TEXT  DEFAULT 'The economic impact of open-source AI models',
    @quality_threshold FLOAT DEFAULT 0.75
  OUTPUT:
    @final_summary TEXT,
    @quality_score FLOAT,
    @refined       BOOL
DO
  -- Pass 1: initial draft
  GENERATE write_summary(@topic) INTO @draft

  -- Evaluate quality; parse the returned decimal string to a float
  GENERATE evaluate_summary(@draft) INTO @score_str
  CALL to_float(@score_str) INTO @quality_score

  EVALUATE @quality_score
    WHEN > @quality_threshold THEN
      @final_summary := @draft
      @refined := FALSE
      COMMIT @final_summary WITH quality = @quality_score, refined = 'no'

    OTHERWISE
      GENERATE refine_summary(@draft, @topic) INTO @final_summary
      @refined := TRUE
      COMMIT @final_summary WITH quality = @quality_score, refined = 'yes'
  END

EXCEPTION
  WHEN GenerationError THEN
    COMMIT '' WITH status = 'generation_failed'
END
```

     | ============================================================
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 4
     | Tokens: 480 in / 401 out
     | Latency: 4794ms

     |         return None
